108 BE IT ENACTED BY THE COUNCIL OF THE DISTRICT OF COLUMBIA, That this
109 act may be cited as the “Fiscal Year 2026 Budget Support Act of 2025”.
110 TITLE I. GOVERNMENT DIRECTION AND SUPPORT
111 SUBTITLE A. LIMITATIONS ON LIABILITY AGAINST THE DISTRICT
112 Sec. 1001. Short title.
113 This subtitle may be cited as the “Limitations on Liability Against the District of
114 Columbia Act of 2025”.
115 Sec. 1002. Limitations on liability for unliquidated damage claims against the District.
116 (a) The liability of the District of Columbia, including its instrumentalities, for
117 unliquidated damages to persons or property arising out of the same incident or occurrence shall
118 not exceed $500,000 regardless of the number of claimants or beneficiaries who share in the
119 award; except, that the liability of the District of Columbia for unliquidated damages to persons
120 or property arising from intentional wrongful acts or omissions shall not exceed $1 million for all
121 claims arising out of the same incident or occurrence, regardless of the number of claimants or
122 beneficiaries who share in the award.
5

123 (b) No portion of an award against the District for unliquidated damages to a person may
124 include noneconomic damages unless a claimant first establishes that the claimant incurred
125 reasonable and necessary medical expenses of more than $10,000 due to the act or omission of
126 the District of Columbia for which the claim is made, except in the case of an injury resulting in
127 permanent disfigurement or death or resulting from an intentional wrongful act.
128 (c) This section shall apply to all claims or causes of action against the District of
129 Columbia, including its instrumentalities, filed in any court or other tribunal of competent
130 jurisdiction on or after October 1, 2025.
131 Sec. 1003. Limited application of the collateral source rule to actions against the District.
132 In addition to any other limitation under law, in any action against the District of
133 Columbia, including its instrumentalities, to recover damages for personal injury, survivorship,
134 or wrongful death, where the plaintiff seeks to recover for the cost of medical care, dental care,
135 custodial care, or rehabilitation services, only evidence of actual amounts paid or required to be
136 paid by or on behalf of the plaintiff shall be admissible for consideration by a judge or jury in
137 determining damages.
138 Sec. 1004. The District of Columbia Employee Non-Liability Act, effective July 14, 1960
139 (Pub. L. 86-654, 74 Stat. 519; D.C. Official Code § 2-411 et seq.), is amended as follows:
140 (a) Section 2 (D.C. Official Code § 2-411) is amended by adding a new paragraph (6A) to
141 read as follows:
142 “(6A) “Gross negligence” means such an extreme deviation from the ordinary
143 standard of care so as to support a finding of wanton, willful, and reckless disregard or conscious
144 indifference for the rights and safety of others. In assessing whether there is such an extreme
6

145 deviation from the ordinary standard of care, due deference shall be given to the mission giving
146 rise to the emergency run and the need to respond expeditiously under the circumstances.”
147 (b) Section 3 (D.C. Official Code § 2-412) is amended as follows:
148 (1) The existing text is designated as subsection (a).
149 (2) A new subsection (b) is added to read as follows:
150 “(b) In any suit at law that arises out of the operation of a District of Columbia
151 emergency vehicle on an emergency run, a party’s contributory negligence shall be a complete
152 bar to recovery by the party. To establish contributory negligence, the District shall not be
153 required to prove that the party was grossly negligent, and the party’s failure to yield to a vehicle
154 on an emergency run that has its lights and sirens activated shall constitute contributory
155 negligence as a matter of law.”.
156 SUBTITLE B. COMMUNITY AFFAIRS
157 Sec. 1011. Short title.
158 This subtitle may be cited as the “Community Affairs Amendment Act of 2025”.
159 Sec. 1012. Cultural and community affairs grants.
160 (a)(1) The Mayor may issue grants to individuals and organizations that provide services
161 to District residents to support cultural affairs, community relations, and community
162 partnerships.
163 (2) Grants issued under this subsection shall be administered pursuant to the
164 requirements set forth in the Grant Administration Act of 2013, effective December 24, 2013
165 (D.C. Law 20-61; D.C. Official Code § 1-328.11 et seq.).
166 (b) The Mayor shall provide centralized review and approval of grants issued pursuant to:
7

167 (1) Section 3(10) of the Office and Commission on African Affairs Act of 2006,
168 effective June 8, 2006 (D.C Law 16-111; D.C. Official Code § 2-1392(10));
169 (2) Section 3(b)(3) of the Office on African American Affairs Establishment Act
170 of 2017, effectively February 17, 2018 (D.C. Law 22-59; D.C. Official Code § 2-1398.02(b)(3));
171 (3) Section 304(c)(9) of the Office on Asian and Pacific Islander Affairs
172 Establishment Act of 2001, effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 2-
173 1373(c)(9));
174 (4) Section 3(3) of the Office on Caribbean Community Affairs Establishment
175 Act of 2020, effective May 6, 2020 (D.C. Law 23-87; D.C Official Code § 3-1452(3));
176 (5) Section 303(10) of the District of Columbia Latino Community Development
177 Act, effective September 29, 1976 (D.C. Law 1-86; D.C. Code § 2-1313(10));
178 (6) Sections 4(b)(11), (11A), and (12) and 4a of the Office of Gay, Lesbian,
179 Bisexual, and Transgender Affairs Act of 2006, effective April 4, 2006 (D.C. Law 16-89; D.C.
180 Official Code §§ 2-1383(b)(11), (11A), and (12), and 2-1384);
181 (7) Section 3(b)(2)(L) of the Office on Ex-Offender Affairs and Commission on
182 Re-entry and Ex-Offender Affairs Establishment Act of 2006, effective March 8, 2007 (D.C.
183 Law 16-243; D.C. Official Code § 24-1302(b)(2)(L)); and
184 (8) Section 704(6A) of the Office of Veterans Affairs Establishment Act of 2001,
185 effective October 3, 2001 (D.C. Law 14-28; D.C. Official Code § 49-1003(6A)).
186 Sec. 1013. The Commission on Fathers, Men, and Boys Establishment Act of 2014,
187 effective February 26, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-155; D.C. Official Code § 1072 et seq.), is repealed.
8

188 Sec. 1014. Section 3(b)(2)(L) of the Office on Ex-Offender Affairs and the Commission
189 on Re-Entry and Ex-Offender Affairs Establishment Act of 2006, effective March 8, 2007 (D.C.

192 “(L) Have the authority to establish and implement a program to support the
193 employment of returning citizens through grants to employers; provided, that:”.

196 SUBTITLE C. SURPLUS PROPERTY FUND
197 Sec. 1021. Short title.
198 This subtitle may be cited as the “Surplus Property Sales Fund Amendment Act of 2025”.
199 Sec. 1022. Section 805 of the Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective
200 October 22, 2015 (D.C. Law 21-36; D.C. Official Code § 2-358.05), is amended as follows:
201 (a) Subsection (c) is amended to read as follows:
202 “(c) Money in the Fund shall be used to pay the operational costs of OCP.”
203 (b) Subsection (d) is amended to read as follows:
204 “(d) Any money remaining available in the Fund at the end of a fiscal year, as determined

208 SUBTITLE D. CYBERSECURITY AND ARTIFICIAL INTELLIGENCE
209 Sec. 1031. Short title.
9

210 This subtitle may be cited as the “Office of the Chief Technology Officer Amendment

212 Sec. 1032. The Office of the Chief Technology Officer Establishment Act of 1998,
213 effective March 26, 1999 (D.C. Law 12-175; D.C. Official Code § 1-1401 et seq.), is amended as
214 follows:
215 (a) Section 1812a (D.C. Official Code § 1-1401.01) is amended to read as follows:
216 “Sec. 1812a. Definitions.
217 “For the purposes of this act, the term:
218 “(a) “Information technology” includes artificial intelligence.
219 “(b) “Office” means the Office of the Chief Technology Officer established by section

222 (1) Paragraph (1) is amended by striking the phrase “Issue regulations governing
223 the acquisition, use, and management” and inserting the phrase “Issue and enforce policies,
224 standards, and regulations governing the acquisition, use, management, and security” in its place.
225 (2) New paragraphs (7A), (7B), and (7C) are added to read as follows:

227 government’s information technology systems and assets;
228 “(7B) Protect the District government’s information technology systems and
229 assets, and the information on those systems and assets, from cyberattacks, breaches, theft,
230 damage, disruption, and misdirection;
10

231 “(7C) Detect, mitigate, defend, remediate, and respond to cybersecurity threats

237 (1) The lead-in language is amended by striking the number “3” and inserting the
238 number “4” in its place.
239 (2) Paragraph (2) is amended by striking the phrase “; and” and inserting a
240 semicolon in its place.
241 (3) Paragraph (3) is amended by striking the period and inserting the phrase “;
242 and” in its place.
243 (4) A new paragraph (4) is added to read as follows:
244 “(4) Security Services, which shall be responsible for:
245 “(A) Leading the District government’s cybersecurity efforts, including
246 managing the risk of cyberattacks and breaches, and detecting, mitigating, defending, and
247 responding to cybersecurity threats and security vulnerabilities in the District government’s

249 “(B) Establishing an information technology risk management and

251 development, implementation, and management of a formal process for systems authorization
252 that includes a risk assessment, categorization of information and systems, selection and
11

253 implementation of controls, assessment of controls, authorization to operate, and continuous

257 “(a) Except as provided in subsection (b) of this section, the authority of the Office shall
258 apply to all District government agencies, including independent agencies.
259 “(b)(1) The authority of the Office under sections 1813 and 1814 shall not apply to the
260 Council or the Office of the District of Columbia Auditor.
261 “(2) Notwithstanding paragraph (1) of this subsection, the Office and the Council

264 “(A) Manage, assist, or coordinate the operations of the information and

266 and
267 “(B) Carry out any other responsibility for the Council or the Office of the
268 District of Columbia Auditor that the Office may carry out for other District government
269 agencies.”.
270 SUBTITLE E. TELEWORK POLICIES
271 Sec. 1041. Short title.
272 This subtitle may be cited as the “Telework Policy Amendment Act of 2025”.
273 Sec. 1042. The District of Columbia Government Comprehensive Merit Personnel Act of
274 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C. Official Code § 1-601.01 et seq.), is
275 amended by adding a new section 201a to read as follows:
12

276 “Sec. 201a. Telework.
277 “(a) The Mayor may establish a telework policy that applies to all agencies.
278 “(b) No personnel authority or agency shall establish its own telework policy, unless
279 authorized by the Mayor, and no personnel authority or agency shall implement a telework
280 policy other than the policy established by the Mayor pursuant to subsection (a) of this section,
281 unless authorized by the Mayor.
282 “(c) At the request of the Mayor, each agency shall submit a report to the Mayor that
283 includes information on the use of telework by the agency’s employees.
284 “(d) The Mayor may audit agencies’ implementation of the telework policy established
285 pursuant to subsection (a) or (b) of this section and employees’ utilization of telework to ensure
286 compliance with the telework policy and this section.
287 “(e) No personnel authority or agency may enter into a collective bargaining agreement
288 that includes or requires a telework policy.
289 “(f) For the purposes of this section, the term:
290 “(1) “Agency” shall have the meaning set forth in section 301(1) and shall include
291 agencies not otherwise subject to this act, except for the Council and agencies of the legislative
292 branch of the District government.
293 “(2) “Routine telework” means a telework arrangement in which an employee is
294 authorized to telework on an ongoing basis.
295 “(3) “Situational telework” means a temporary telework arrangement in which the
296 employee is authorized to telework due to specific, temporary personal circumstances which
297 prevent the employee from working from a District government office or worksite or for another
298 specific, temporary circumstance approved by the personnel authority.
13

299 “(4)(A) “Telework” means an arrangement in which an employee performs
300 employment duties at their home or other location that is not a District government office or
301 worksite during hours that constitute their official tour of duty.
302 “(B) The term “telework” includes both routine telework and situational
303 telework.”.
304 “(g) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
305 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), may issue
306 rules to implement the provisions of this section.”.
307 SUBTITLE F. DISTRICT EMPLOYEE PAID PARENTAL, FAMILY, AND
308 MEDICAL LEAVE
309 Sec. 1051. Short title.
310 This subtitle may be cited as the “District Employee Paid Parental, Family, and Medical
311 Leave Amendment Act of 2025”.
312 Sec. 1052. The District of Columbia Government Comprehensive Merit Personnel Act of
313 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C. Official Code § 1-601.01 et seq.), is
314 amended as follows:
315 (a) Section 1204 (D.C. Official Code § 1-612.04) is amended as follows:
316 (1) Paragraph (4) is amended to read as follows:
317 “(4)(A) “Eligible employee” means a District government employee, including an
318 employee of an independent agency; provided, that for the purposes of using paid family leave or
319 paid medical leave, the term “eligible employee” means a District government employee,
320 including an employee of an independent agency, has worked for the District government for at
14

321 least 180 days, without a break in service, as of the date on which the paid family leave or paid
322 medical leave will be used.
323 “(B) The term “eligible employee” does not include:
324 “(i) A temporary employee appointed for less than 90 days; or
325 “(ii) An employee with intermittent employment.”.
326 (2) Paragraph (5) is amended as follows:
327 (A) Subparagraph (B) is amended by striking the semicolon at the end and
328 inserting the phrase “; or” in its place.
329 (B) Subparagraph (C) is amended to read as follows:
330 “(C) A spouse or domestic partner.”.
331 (C) Subparagraphs (D) and (E) are repealed.
332 (b) Section 1204a (D.C. Official Code § 1-612.04a) is amended as follows:
333 (1) Subsection (a)(1)(B) is amended by striking the phrase “8 workweeks” and
334 inserting the phrase “2 workweeks” in its place.
335 (2) A new subsection (c-1) is added to read as follows:
336 “(c-1)(1) To the extent practicable, an eligible employee shall, before using paid leave,
337 provide written notice to their personnel authority or agency of the need for the use of paid leave
338 and of the expected date or dates on which the employee intends to use paid leave.
339 “(2) If the employee plans to use paid leave on an intermittent basis, the written
340 notice shall, to the extent practicable, include a schedule of the expected hours during which the
341 employee intends to use paid leave.
15

342 “(3) The written notice shall include a reason for the use of paid leave, within the
343 parameters of the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996, approved August
344 21, 1996 (Pub. L. No. 104-191; 110 Stat. 1936).
345 “(4) If the use of paid leave is foreseeable, the written notice shall be provided at
346 least 10 days, or as early as possible, in advance of the use of the paid leave.
347 “(5) If the use of paid leave is unforeseeable, a notification, either oral or written,
348 shall be provided before the start of the work shift for which the paid leave is being used.
349 “(6) In the case of an emergency resulting in the use of paid leave without the
350 opportunity to provide prior notification, the eligible employee, or another individual on behalf
351 of the eligible employee, shall notify the Mayor, either orally or in writing, within 48 hours after
352 the emergency occurs.
353 “(7) If the agency determines that the use of paid leave is likely to interfere with
354 the operations of the agency, the agency and eligible employee shall engage in good-faith
355 negotiations on alternate dates or hours for the use of the paid leave. The agency may deny the
356 use of paid leave under this section if an employee does not agree to a reasonable request to
357 revise the dates or hours for the use of the paid leave.”.
358 (3) Subsection (d)(2) is amended to read as follows:
359 “(2) If a probationary employee voluntarily separates in violation of the 1-year
360 continuation of service agreement, the individual shall be indebted to the District government for
361 the salary paid during the leave period. Indebtedness incurred pursuant to this paragraph may be
362 treated in whole or in part as an erroneous payment pursuant to Title XXIX.”.
363 (4) A new subsection (d-1) is added to read as follows:
16

364 “(d-1)(1) An employee, other than an employee serving in a probationary capacity, using
365 paid parental, family, or medical leave shall be required to enter into a continuation of service
366 agreement. The continuation of service agreement shall require the employee to continue to
367 serve as a District employee for 12 weeks after the use of the paid parental, family, or medical
368 leave.
369 “(2) If the employee voluntarily separates in violation of the continuation of
370 service agreement, the individual shall be indebted to the District government for the salary paid
371 during the leave period. Indebtedness incurred pursuant to this paragraph may be treated in
372 whole or in part as an erroneous payment pursuant to Title XXIX.”.

408 SUBTITLE I. RETROACTIVE PAY INCREASES
409 Sec. 1081. Short title.
18

410 This subtitle may be cited as the “Retroactive Pay Increase Restriction Amendment Act
411 of 2025”.
412 Sec. 1082. Definitions.
413 For the purposes of this subtitle, the term “covered agency” means an agency, office, or
414 instrumentality of the District government and independent agencies, as defined in section
415 301(13) of the CMPA (D.C. Official Code § 1-603.01(13)); except, that the term “covered
416 agency” does not include the District of Columbia Housing Authority, the District of Columbia
417 Housing Finance Agency, the District of Columbia Water and Sewer Authority, the Not-for-
418 Profit Hospital Corporation, the University of the District of Columbia, or the Washington
419 Convention and Sports Authority.
420 Sec. 1083. Restriction on certain retroactive pay increases.
421 Notwithstanding any other provision of law, rule, collective bargaining agreement,
422 memorandum of understanding, side letter, settlement, or arbitration award, no increase in salary,
423 wages, or benefits at a covered agency shall be authorized or provided retroactively for Fiscal
424 Year 2024 or Fiscal Year 2025, except for:
425 (a) An increase provided for by a law enacted, resolution approved, or rule issued before
426 May 15, 2025;
427 (b) An increase included in a salary, wage, or benefit provision that was included in:
428 (1) A collective bargaining agreement with respect to which the parties to the
429 agreement reached agreement before May 15, 2025; or
430 (2) A memorandum of understanding or side letter entered into before May 15,
431 2025; or
19

432 (c) An increase required by a final arbitration award that is not still subject to judicial
433 review, if the arbitration was initiated before May 15, 2025; and
434 (d) An increase provided to an employee on an individualized basis pursuant to a law,
435 resolution, rule, salary, wage, or benefit provision, or arbitration award referred to in paragraph
436 (2) of this subsection, based on the employee’s performance or another factor authorized by such
437 law, resolution, rule, collective bargaining agreement, memorandum of understanding, side
438 letter, settlement, or arbitration award.
439 Sec. 1084. Rules.
440 To the extent a personnel authority is authorized by the District of Columbia Government
441 Comprehensive Merit Personnel Act of 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-139; D.C.
442 Official Code § 1-601.01 et seq.), or other law to issue rules to administer the salary or benefits
443 program of a covered agency, the personnel authority for the covered agency may, pursuant to
444 Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82
445 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), issue rules to implement this subtitle with respect
446 to the covered agency.
447 Sec. 1085. Applicability.
448 This subtitle shall apply as of May 15, 2025.

794 (j) New sections 8a and 8b are added to read as follows:
795 “Sec. 8a. Seizure of unlawfully vended merchandise and associated vending property.
796 “(a) The Mayor may, upon issuance of a notice of infraction and seizure and without
797 providing a prior opportunity to be heard, seize any merchandise being sold from public space,
798 as well as any property, including vending carts and equipment, used to vend the merchandise, if:
799 “(1) The person:
800 “(A) Is vending the merchandise without a required authorization;
801 “(B) Fails to provide proof of a required authorization upon the request of
802 the enforcement officer; or
803 “(C) Offers or provides to an enforcement officer an altered or falsified
804 required authorization.
805 “(2) An altered or falsified required authorization is displayed at the location
806 where the merchandise is being vended.
807 “(b)(1) If the Mayor seizes a person’s merchandise or property pursuant to subsection (a),
808 the Mayor shall hand deliver the notice of infraction and seizure to the vendor, and the notice of
36

809 infraction and seizure shall be treated for purposes of answering, hearing, adjudication, decision,
810 and appeal as a notice of infraction under section 201 of the Department of Consumer and
811 Regulatory Affairs Civil Infractions Act of 1985 (“Civil Infractions Act”), effective October 5,
812 1985 (D.C. Law 6-42; D.C. Official Code § 2-1802.01).
813 “(2) If the person vending the merchandise is different than the individual listed in
814 DLCP’s records as the business owner, the Mayor shall also provide the notice of infraction and
815 seizure, by first-class mail, no later than 5 business days after property is seized, to the last
816 known address of the business owner in DLCP’s records. If DLCP has no record of the business
817 license owner, providing the notice of infraction and seizure to the person vending the
818 merchandise shall be considered constructive notice to the owner of the merchandise.
819 “(3) A notice of infraction and seizure issued pursuant to paragraph (1) or (2) of
820 this subsection shall include the information required by section 201(b) of the Civil Infractions
821 Act (D.C. Official Code § 2-1802.01(b)) and the following additional information:
822 “(A) A description of the action taken by the Mayor, including a
823 description of the seized merchandise and property;
824 “(B) A statement that the respondent has a right to request an expedited
825 hearing by making a request for an expedited hearing in writing within 3 business days after
826 service of the notice;
827 “(C) The method by which the respondent may recover the merchandise or
828 property that was seized, if applicable;
829 “(D) The date by which the respondent must recover the merchandise or
830 property before it may be subject to forfeiture and disposal pursuant to this section, which date
831 shall be at least 21 days after the date of seizure, except where the merchandise or property is
37

832 likely to perish or be greatly reduced in value after seizure or the expense of keeping the
833 merchandise or property is disproportionate to its value;
834 “(E) A statement that the merchandise or property shall be considered
835 forfeited and will be sold or otherwise disposed of if it is not recovered by the respondent within
836 21 days of seizure; except as provided in subparagraph (F) of this paragraph; and
837 “(F) A statement that if the merchandise or property is likely to perish or
838 be greatly reduced in value by or after its seizure, or the expense of keeping the merchandise or
839 property is disproportionate to its value, the Mayor may immediately sell or otherwise dispose of
840 the merchandise or property.
841 “(c) If a respondent requests an expedited hearing within 3 business days after service of
842 the notice of infraction and seizure, the Office of Administrative Hearings shall conduct the
843 hearing within 3 business days after receipt of the request and shall issue a decision within 10
844 business days after the hearing.
845 “(d)(1) When merchandise or property is seized pursuant to this section, the Mayor shall:
846 “(A) Place the merchandise and property in an area designated by the
847 Mayor for safe storage until disposition;
848 “(B) Create an inventory of the seized merchandise and property with a
849 description of all merchandise and property seized; and
850 “(C) Assign an identification number to each item of merchandise and
851 property seized, except as provided in paragraph (2) of this subsection.
852 “(2) For the purposes of this subsection:
853 “(A) A sum of currency shall be deemed to be a single item of property;
854 and
38

855 “(B) Identical items may be identified by a single identification number;
856 provided, that the quantity of the item is listed with the identification number.
857 “(e)(1) If seized merchandise or property is likely to perish or be greatly reduced in value
858 by or after its seizure, or the expense of keeping the merchandise or property is disproportionate
859 to its value, the Mayor may immediately sell or otherwise dispose of the merchandise or
860 property.
861 “(2) If, pursuant to paragraph (1) of this subsection, the Mayor sells seized
862 merchandise or property, the sale proceeds shall become substitute property for the original
863 seized merchandise or property and shall be subject to forfeiture in accordance with the standards
864 and procedures set forth in this section.
865 “(3) If, pursuant to paragraph (1) of this subsection, the Mayor discards seized
866 property, the fair market value of the discarded property before it is discarded shall become
867 substitute property for the original seized property and shall be subject to forfeiture in
868 accordance with the standards and procedures set forth in this section.
869 “(4) The Mayor shall maintain records of merchandise and property sold or
870 otherwise disposed of under this subsection, including the purchase price of any merchandise or
871 property sold, and shall maintain the disposition records with the associated inventory of seized
872 merchandise and property.
873 “(f) The vendor, or the owner if different from the vendor, whose merchandise or
874 property is seized pursuant to this section, or a person duly authorized by such person, may
875 secure the release of the merchandise or property by paying the seizure fee, transportation fee,
876 and storage fee, if any, for the merchandise or property.
39

877 “(g) The person to whom the merchandise or property is returned shall acknowledge
878 receipt and possession of each item of returned merchandise or property by reference to the
879 specific property identification number assigned to the item.
880 “(h) A person whose merchandise or property is seized pursuant to this subsection shall
881 be entitled to a refund of the seizure fee, transportation fee, and storage fees if the violations or
882 infractions giving rise to the seizure are dismissed or overturned and such dismissal or
883 overturning is neither subject to appeal nor under appeal by the District.
884 “(i) If a person whose merchandise or property is seized pursuant to this section does not
885 claim the seized merchandise or property by the date set forth in the notice of infraction and
886 seizure, the merchandise and property shall be deemed forfeited and the Mayor may sell, destroy,
887 or otherwise dispose of the merchandise and property.
888 “(j)(1) A person whose merchandise or property is seized pursuant to this section and
889 fails to reclaim their merchandise or property within 21 days after seizure, or such later date as
890 may be set forth in the notice of infraction and seizure, or such earlier date in the case of seized
891 merchandise or property that is likely to perish or be greatly reduced in value by or after its
892 seizure or for which the expense of keeping the merchandise or property is disproportionate to its
893 value, and whose property is thereafter sold, destroyed, or otherwise disposed of by the Mayor
894 shall nevertheless be entitled to recover the fair market value of any merchandise or property
895 sold, destroyed, or otherwise disposed of if:
896 “(A) The person timely requests a hearing on the applicable notice of
897 infraction and seizure;
40

898 “(B) The administrative law judge issues an order dismissing the notice of
899 infraction and seizure or finding no violation and the order is neither subject to appeal nor under
900 appeal by the District; and
901 “(C) The person establishes the merchandise or property’s fair market
902 value by a preponderance of the evidence.
903 “(2) If the Mayor has sold the merchandise or property, the price paid by a good-
904 faith purchaser, other than the person whose property was seized, shall establish a rebuttable
905 presumption of the fair market value of the property.
906 “(k) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
907 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2- 501, et seq.) may issue
908 rules to implement this subsection.
909 “Sec. 8b. Towing and impoundment of unlawfully operating vending trucks.
910 “(a)(1) The Mayor may, upon issuance of a notice of infraction and impoundment and
911 without providing a prior opportunity to be heard, seize, tow, and impound:
912 “(A) A vending truck if the vending truck owner, vending truck operator,
913 or an agent or employee of the vending truck owner or vending truck operator:
914 “(i) Is vending from the vending truck without a required
915 authorization;
916 “(ii) Provides to an enforcement officer an altered or falsified
917 required authorization;
918 “(iii) Fails to provide proof of a required authorization upon
919 request by an enforcement officer; or
920 “(iv) Operates the vending truck illegally in public space; or
41

921 “(B) A vending truck that:
922 “(i) Is illegally parked in public space; or
923 “(ii) Displays an altered or falsified required authorization.
924 “(C) A vehicle that is illegally parked in a vending truck vending zone.
925 “(2) If towing services are not immediately available, the Mayor may immobilize
926 the vehicle until towing services are available.
927 “(b)(1) If the Mayor impounds a vending truck under this subsection, the Mayor shall, as
928 further described in this subsection, provide a written notice of infraction and impoundment to:
929 “(A) The vending truck owner;
930 “(B) The vending truck operator if different than the food truck owner;
931 and
932 “(C) Any lienholders of record of the vending truck, if applicable.
933 “(2) A notice of infraction and impoundment issued pursuant to this section shall
934 be treated for purposes of answering, hearing, adjudication, decision, and appeal as a notice of
935 infraction under section 201 of the Department of Consumer and Regulatory Affairs Civil
936 Infractions Act of 1985 (“Civil Infractions Act”), effective October 5, 1985 (D.C. Law 6-42;
937 D.C. Official Code § 2-1802.01).
938 “(3) A notice of infraction and impoundment issued pursuant to this section shall
939 include the information required by section 201(b) of the Civil Infractions Act (D.C. Official
940 Code § 2-1802.01(b)) and the following additional information:
941 “(A) The vehicle identification number of the vending truck, if applicable;
942 “(B) The amount of any fees imposed or to be imposed;
42

943 “(C) A statement that the vending truck will be kept for 72 hours and a
944 description of the procedures for reclaiming the vending truck, which shall be the procedures
945 described in section 9 of the Removal and Disposition of Abandoned and Other Unlawfully
946 Parked Vehicles Reform Act of 2003, effective October 28, 2003 (D.C. Law 15-35; D.C. Official
947 Code § 50-2421.09);
948 “(D) The date by which the person must reclaim the vending truck before
949 it shall be subject to forfeiture and disposal pursuant to this section, which date shall be at least
950 28 days after the date of impoundment;
951 “(E) A statement that the vending truck shall be considered forfeited and
952 will be sold or otherwise disposed of if it is not reclaimed by the expiration of the reclamation
953 period, and that any food, merchandise, or equipment on the vending truck shall also be
954 considered forfeited and disposed of in accordance with section 8a; and
955 “(F) A statement that the person has the right to request an expedited
956 hearing from the Office of Administrative Hearings, by making a request for an expedited
957 hearing in writing within 3 business days after service of the notice.
958 “(4)(A) The maximum rates that may be charged for the towing of a vending
959 truck pursuant to this section shall be as follows:
960 “(i) $750 for preparation, hoist, and tow (including use of a roll-
961 back or wheel lift) to a location within the District;
962 “(ii) $20 per mile for towing beyond the District line; and
963 “(iii) $75 for storage per 24-hour period or part thereof.
964 “(B) Upon written request, and if approved by the Director of the
965 Department of Licensing and Consumer Protection, the private tow company employed to
43

966 remove a vending truck pursuant to this section may charge a towing fee greater than what is set
967 forth in this subsection, but no greater than three times the amount.
968 “(5)(A) The notice of infraction and impoundment shall be provided by hand to
969 the vending truck operator, if the vending truck operator is present at the time the notice is
970 issued. If a vending truck operator is not present at the time the notice is issued, the notice shall
971 be posted in a prominent location on the vending truck.
972 “(B) The notice of infraction and impoundment shall be provided to the
973 vending truck owner, if different than the vending truck operator, by first-class mail, no later
974 than 5 days after the vehicle is seized, towed, or impounded, to the last known address of the
975 vending truck owner, as that information is indicated in the records of the Department of Motor
976 Vehicles or in the records of the appropriate agency of the jurisdiction where the vending truck is
977 registered, if applicable.
978 “(C) If neither the vending truck owner nor a vending truck operator is
979 present at the time the notice of infraction and impoundment is issued, and the vending truck
980 does not have a license plate attached to it, then the notice shall be posted on DLCP’s or a
981 District government webpage dedicated to the posting of such notices.
982 “(D) A notice to a lienholder of record, if applicable, shall be provided by
983 first-class mail to their last known address as that information is indicated in the records of the
984 Department of Motor Vehicles or in the records of the appropriate agency of the jurisdiction
985 where the vending truck is registered.
986 “(6) If a respondent requests an expedited hearing within 3 business days after
987 service of the notice, the Office of Administrative Hearings shall conduct the hearing within 3
44

988 business days after receipt of the request and shall issue a decision within 10 business days after
989 the hearing.
990 “(7) After the vending truck has been held for 72 hours in accordance with
991 subsection (b)(3)(C), a vending truck owner, or a person duly authorized by a vending truck
992 owner, may secure the release of an impounded vending truck by becoming licensed to operate
993 in the District of Columbia, paying the impoundment fee, towing fee, immobilization fee, if
994 applicable, for the impounded vending truck, and furnishing proof of entitlement to possession of
995 the vehicle, including proof of licensure to operate a vehicle, title, and registration.
996 “(8) A vending truck owner shall be entitled to a refund of the impoundment fee,
997 towing fee, immobilization fee, if applicable, and no more than 3 business days storage costs, if
998 applicable, if the violations or infractions giving rise to the impoundment are dismissed or
999 overturned and such dismissal or overturning is neither subject to appeal nor under appeal by the
1000 District.
1001 “(9) A vending truck impounded under this section may be disposed of pursuant
1002 to section 10 of the Removal and Disposition of Abandoned and Other Unlawfully Parked
1003 Vehicles Reform Act of 2003, effective October 28, 2003 (D.C. Law 15-35; D.C. Official Code
1004 § 50-2421.10).
1005 “(10) The Mayor may contract with, or otherwise engage, a private entity to tow,
1006 impound, store, and release vending trucks pursuant to this section and to perform ancillary
1007 services.
1008 “(11) For the purposes of this subsection, the term “enforcement officer” shall
1009 have the meaning set forth in section 9(d)(3)(B).
45

1010 “(12) The Mayor, pursuant to Title I of the District of Columbia Administrative
1011 Procedure Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.),
1012 may issue rules to implement this subsection.”.

1137 excluding weekends, holidays, and days of council recess. If the Council does not approve or
1138 disapprove the proposed rules, by resolution, within the 60-day review period, the proposed rules
1139 shall be deemed disapproved.” and inserting the phrase “by the Mayor.” in its place.
1140 Sec. 2043. Section 4935(3)(C) of the Department of Health Functions Clarification Act of

1144 SUBTITLE F. TIPPED MINIMUM WAGE
1145 Sec. 2051. Short title.
1146 This subtitle may be cited as the “Tipped Minimum Wage Amendment Act of 2025”.
51

1147 Sec. 2052. The Minimum Wage Act Revision Act of 1992, effective March 25, 1993
1148 (D.C. Law 9-248; D.C. Official Code § 32-1001 et seq.), is amended as follows:
1149 (a) Section 4(f) (D.C. Official Code § 32-1003(f)) is amended to read as follows:
1150 “(f)(1) The minimum hourly wage required to be paid by an employer to an employee
1151 who receives gratuities (“tipped minimum wage”), provided that the employee actually receives
1152 gratuities in an amount at least equal to the difference between the hourly wage paid and the
1153 minimum hourly wage as set by subsection (a) of this section, shall be as of October 1, 2025,
1154 $5.95.
1155 “(2) Beginning on July 1, 2026, and no later than July 1 of each successive year,
1156 the tipped minimum wage shall be increased in proportion to the annual average increase, if any,
1157 in the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers in the Washington Metropolitan
1158 Statistical Area published by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States Department of
1159 Labor for the previous calendar year. Any increase under this paragraph shall be adjusted to the
1160 nearest multiple of $.05.”.

1162 SUBTITLE G. CARD GAMING
1163 Sec. 2061. Short title.
1164 This subtitle may be cited as the “Poker and Blackjack Gaming Authorization Act of
1165 2025”.
1166 Sec. 2062. The Law to Legalize Lotteries, Daily Numbers Games, and Bingo and Raffles
1167 for Charitable Purposes in the District of Columbia, effective March 10, 1981 (D.C. Law 3-172;
1168 D.C. Official Code § 36-601.01 passim), is amended as follows:
52

1169 (a) Section 3 (D.C. Official Code § 22-1716) is amended by striking the phrase “and
1170 sports wagering” and insert the phrase “sports wagering, poker, and blackjack” in its place.
1171 (b) Section 3 (D.C. Official Code § 22-1717) is amended by striking the phrase “game of
1172 skill machines” and inserting the phrase “game of skill machines, poker, and blackjack” in its
1173 place.
1174 (c) A new title V is added to read as follows:
1175 “TITLE V. CARD GAMING; POKER AND BLACKJACK.
1176 “Sec. 501 Definitions.
1177 “For the purposes of this title the term:
1178 “(1) “ABCA” means the Alcoholic Beverage and Cannabis Administration.
1179 “(2) “ABCB” means the Alcoholic Beverage and Cannabis Board.
1180 “(3) “Authorized establishment” means an eligible establishment where a card
1181 gaming facility is authorized to operate under this title.
1182 “(4) “Blackjack gross gaming revenue” means the total amount wagered by
1183 players on blackjack, including any variations thereof, less total winnings paid out to players, not
1184 including promotions, credits or other noncash items.
1185 “(5) “Card game” means blackjack or poker, including any authorized variations
1186 of blackjack or poker.
1187 “(6) “Card gaming” means wagering on a card game.
1188 “(7) “Card gaming facility” means a location where wagering on card games is
1189 authorized under this title.
1190 “(8) “Card gaming operations” means the operation of an authorized card gaming
1191 facility.
53

1192 “(9) “CFO” means the Chief Financial Officer of the District of Columbia.
1193 “(10) “Eligible establishment” means a business licensed by the Alcoholic
1194 Beverage and Cannabis Board that holds an on-premises retailer’s license class C/H, D/H or
1195 arena CX.
1196 “(11) “Office” means the Office of Lottery and Gaming.
1197 “(12) “Operator” means a person who holds a card gaming facility operator
1198 license.
1199 “(13) “Person” means a natural person or entity.
1200 “(14) “Poker gross gaming revenue” means the gross receipts generated from
1201 poker, including any variations thereof, including rake, entry fees, commissions, and similar
1202 amounts paid by players to participate in poker games.
1203 “(15) “Supplier” means a person that:
1204 “(A) Sells or leases, or contracts to sell or lease, card game equipment,
1205 devices, systems, or supplies to an operator; or
1206 “(B) Provides, or contracts to provide, security or surveillance services
1207 required by the Office to an operator;
1208 “(C) Provides management services to an operator.
1209 “(16) “Voluntary exclusion program” means a program operated by the Office
1210 that allows individuals to voluntarily exclude themselves from engaging in card gaming.
1211 “Sec 502. Authorization of card gaming.
1212 “The operation of facilities where wagering on card games occurs, and the wagering on
1213 card games at such facilities, shall be lawful in the District if conducted in accordance with this
1214 title and the rules issued pursuant to this title.
54

1215 “Sec. 503. Card gaming locations.
1216 “(a) Card gaming shall be permitted under this title only at locations authorized by the
1217 Office to be operated as card gaming facilities.
1218 “(b) The Office shall authorize card gaming facilities to be operated only at eligible
1219 establishments.
1220 “(c) Card gaming facilities shall be authorized to be operated only as part of an operator’s
1221 license issued under this title.
1222 “(d) The Office shall, by rule, establish a limit on the number of card gaming facilities
1223 that may be authorized to be operated in the District. In determining this limit, the Office shall
1224 consider the sufficiency of the number of card gaming facilities to serve the public.
1225 “Sec. 504. Operator’s license required; fee.
1226 “(a) No person shall operate a card gaming facility unless the person holds an operator’s
1227 license issued by the Office. An operator’s license shall authorize the licensee to operate card
1228 gaming facilities only at such eligible establishments as shall be authorized on the license. An
1229 operator shall not operate a card gaming facility at a location in the District other than an eligible
1230 establishment authorized on its license.
1231 “(b) To obtain an operator’s license a person shall:
1232 “(1) Complete and submit to the Office an application for an operator’s license in
1233 the manner and form prescribed by the Office;
1234 “(2) Submit any information and documents requested by the Office as part of the
1235 licensing process;
1236 “(3) Satisfactorily pass a background investigation, which may include the
1237 investigation of owners, officers, directors and employees of the applicant;
55

1238 “(4) Satisfactorily pass an onsite inspection of the location or locations where the
1239 applicant proposes to conduct card gaming operations;
1240 “(5) Meet such other standards as the Office may establish by rule; and
1241 “(6) Pay a nonrefundable application fee of $5,000, plus $2,000 for each location
1242 where the applicant proposes to conduct card gaming operations.
1243 “(c) The term of an operator’s license shall be two years.
1244 “(d) A licensee may renew an operator’s license by filing an application with the Office
1245 and providing such information and documents as may be requested by the Office. The
1246 application fee for the renewal of an operator’s license shall be $1,500 plus $500 for each
1247 location where the licensee is currently licensed to operate a card gaming facility.
1248 “(e) As part of a renewal application, a licensee may request authorization to conduct
1249 card gaming operations at additional locations. The applicant shall pay an additional application
1250 fee of $1,000 for each new location requested.
1251 “(f) An operator’s license shall not be transferable to another person, unless approved by
1252 the Office in accordance with rules issued by the Office.
1253 “(g) A person convicted of a disqualifying offense shall not be licensed as an operator by
1254 the Office. The Office shall define disqualifying offense by a rule issued pursuant to this title.
1255 “(h) No employee of the Office or ABCA or member of the ABC Board, or immediate
1256 family member of an employee of the Office or ABCA or member of the ABC Board, may be an
1257 applicant for, have an interest in, or obtain an operator’s license.”.
1258 “(i) A person who has been denied an application for an operator’s license pursuant to
1259 this section or rules issued pursuant this title shall have a right to a hearing before the Office and,
56

1260 in the event of its affirmation of the denial, the right to appeal the decision of the Office to the
1261 Superior Court of the District of Columbia.
1262 “(j) Before issuing, renewing, or authorizing the transfer a license, the Office shall
1263 determine that the applicant is not disqualified because of a conflicting interest in another license
1264 or a supplier permit. The Office shall define conflicting interest and the standards for
1265 disqualification by rules issued pursuant to this title.
1266 “Sec. 505. Designated areas for card gaming operations within authorized establishments.
1267 “(a) Each licensee shall locate its card gaming operations within the premises of an
1268 authorized establishment only in specific areas approved by ABCA and the Office.
1269 “(b) Each licensee shall post a warning sign clearly visible at each point of entry to the
1270 designated areas where card gaming is located in an authorized establishment. The warning sign
1271 shall include:
1272 “(1) The minimum age required to participate in card gaming;
1273 “(2) The contact information for the District’s gambling hotline;
1274 “(3) Information on the voluntary exclusion program; and
1275 “(4) The contact information for the Office for purposes of filing a licensee or
1276 card gaming facility.
1277 “Sec. 506. Card gaming by minors prohibited.
1278 “(a) Neither a licensee nor an authorized establishment shall permit a person under the
1279 age of 18 to participate in card gaming.
1280 “(b) The Office may suspend or revoke a license and issue a fine, in accordance with
1281 section XXX, against a licensee that knowingly allows a person under the age of 18 to participate
1282 in card gaming.
57

1283 “Sec. 507. Voluntary exclusion program.
1284 “Each licensee shall participate in the voluntary exclusion program operated by the
1285 Office.
1286 “Sec. 508. Taxation of card gaming.
1287 “(a) A tax is imposed on all operators licensed by the Office for the operation of a card
1288 gaming facility.
1289 “(b) The rate of tax shall be 25% of the poker gross gaming revenue and 25% of the
1290 blackjack gross gaming revenue from each card gaming facility the operator is authorized to
1291 operate.
1292 “(c) On or before the 20th calendar day of each month, each operator shall file a return
1293 with the CFO, on forms and in the manner prescribed by the CFO, indicating the amount of
1294 poker gross gaming revenue and blackjack gross gaming revenue from the operator’s authorized
1295 card gaming facilities for the preceding calendar month and the amount of tax for which the
1296 operator is liable.
1297 “(d) All funds owed to the District under this section shall be held in trust for the District
1298 in a federally insured depository institution that maintains an office in the District until the funds
1299 are paid to the District.
1300 “(e) Each operator shall keep a record of the poker gross gaming revenue and blackjack
1301 gross gaming revenue in such form as the CFO may require.
1302 “(f) An operator who fails to pay the tax imposed by this section shall be subject to all
1303 collection, enforcement, and administrative provisions applicable to unpaid taxes or fees, as
1304 provided in Chapters 41, 42, 43, and 44 of Title 47 of the District of Columbia Official Code.
58

1305 “(g) Notwithstanding section 47-4406 of the District of Columbia Official Code, the CFO
1306 may disclose the total amount of poker gross gaming revenue and blackjack gross gaming
1307 revenue collected in the periodic estimates and reports of revenues.
1308 “Sec. 509. Rules governing card gaming.
1309 “(a) The CFO, pursuant to title I of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure
1310 Act, approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1204; D.C. Official Code § 2-501 et seq.), shall adopt
1311 rules governing the conditions under which card gaming shall be conducted in the District and
1312 such other rules it deems appropriate to implement or further the purposes of this title.
1313 “(b) The rules issued by the CFO pursuant to subsection (a) of this section shall include:
1314 “(1) Minimum internal control standards, including:
1315 “(A) Financial controls, including rules regarding the proper handling of
1316 cash, accounting procedures, and auditing requirements;
1317 “(B) Security and surveillance requirements, including rules regarding the
1318 monitoring of gaming areas, protecting against theft and cheating, surveillance camera standards,
1319 and recording and monitoring requirements;
1320 “(C) Game integrity standards designed to ensure fair play, accurate
1321 payouts, and compliance with card game rules;
1322 “(D) Employee-related standards and requirements, including background
1323 checks, training, and ethical conduct requirements; and
1324 “(E) Information technology and data security standards and requirements
1325 designed to protect player information and ensure system integrity.
1326 “(2) Minimum and maximum wager amounts;
1327 “(3) The method of accounting to be used by operators;
59

1328 “(4) Requirements and methods of age verification;
1329 “(5) Requirements regarding records required to be maintained by an operator;
1330 “(6) Advertising guidelines, including specific language concerning individuals
1331 under the age of 18; and
1332 “(7) Penalties for a violation of this title or rule issued pursuant to this title.”.
1333 “Sec. 510. Supplier permit.
1334 “(a) No person shall operate as a supplier unless the person holds a supplier permit issued
1335 by the Office.
1336 “(b) The Office shall establish by rule the requirements and standards for issuance of a
1337 supplier permit and may establish a fee for the application for and issuance of a supplier permit.
1338 “(c) No employee of the Office or ABCA or member of the ABC Board, or immediate
1339 family member of an employee of the Office or ABCA or member of the ABC Board, may be an
1340 applicant for, have an interest in, or obtain a supplier’s permit.”.
1341 “Sec. 511. Penalties.
1342 “(a) For a violation of this title or a rule issued pursuant to this title, the Office may take
1343 one or more of the following actions:
1344 “(1) Impose a fine of not more than $50,000;
1345 “(2) Revoke an operator’s license or a supplier’s permit; or
1346 “(3) Suspend an operator’s license or supplier’s permit.
1347 “(b) A person who has been fined or whose license has been revoked or suspended
1348 pursuant to this section shall have a right to a hearing before the Office and, in the event of its
1349 affirmation of the fine, revocation or suspension, whichever applies, the right to appeal the
1350 decision of the Office to the Superior Court of the District of Columbia.
60

1351 “Sec. 512. Audits, investigations, and inspections.
1352 “(a) The Office may conduct audits, investigations, searches, seizures, and other
1353 investigatory and inspection activities appropriate to the implementation and enforcement of this
1354 title and the rules issued pursuant to this title.
1355 “(b) Each applicant for a license, each licensee, each authorized establishment and each
1356 eligible establishment that is seeking to become an authorized establishment shall allow an
1357 authorized member of the Office, an ABCA investigator, or any member of the Metropolitan
1358 Police Department full opportunity to examine at any time during business hours:
1359 “(1) The area of the authorized establishment or eligible establishment where card
1360 gaming operations are conducted or are requested to be authorized to be conducted; and
1361 “(2) The books and records of the applicant, licensee, authorized establishment, or
1362 eligible establishment, including video and audio recordings, wherever stored.
1363 “Sec. 513. Other enforcement authority; seizures.
1364 “(a) The Office, ABCA, or Metropolitan Police Department may request and check the
1365 identification of a person who has played, is playing, or is attempting to play a card game. The
1366 Office or Metropolitan Police Department may seize evidence that substantiates a violation under
1367 this title, which may include seizing the cash awards issued to a person under the age of 18 and
1368 fake identification documents used by a person under the age of 18.
1369 “(b) The Office or Metropolitan Police Department may seize card gaming equipment,
1370 devices, systems, or supplies from a business if:
1371 “(1) A card gaming facility is not authorized to be operated in the business;
1372 “(2) The license of the operator allowing the operator to operate a card gaming
1373 facility at the business has been suspended, revoked, or canceled by the Office;
61

1374 “(3) The business is no longer in existence; or
1375 “(4) The business has been closed by another District government agency.
1376 “Sec. 514. Action by the Attorney General
1377 The Attorney General for the District of Columbia, in the name of the District of
1378 Columbia, may bring an action in the Superior Court of the District of Columbia to enjoin a
1379 person from violating this title or a rule issued pursuant to this title or to seek a civil penalty of
1380 up to $50,000 for a violation of this title or a rule issued pursuant to this title.
1381 “Sec. 515. Other powers and duties of the Office.
1382 “In addition to the other authorities of the Office under this title, the Office shall have the
1383 power to:
1384 “(a) Oversee all card gaming operations authorized under this title, including all persons
1385 conducting or participating in any card gaming operation;
1386 “(b) Employ or contract for such persons to be present during card gaming operations as
1387 are necessary to ensure that such gaming operations are conducted in an orderly fashion and the
1388 highest degree of integrity; and
1389 “(c) Issue subpoenas for the attendance of witnesses before the Office, administer oaths,
1390 and compel production of records or other documents and testimony of such witnesses whenever
1391 in the judgment of the Office it is necessary to do so for the effectual discharge of its duties
1392 under this title.”.

1442 “Subchapter IX-A. Game of skill machines and card gaming.
64

1443 “§ 25-788. Game of skill machine operating requirements.
1444 “A licensee with a game of skill machine endorsement shall:
1445 “(1) Not allow or permit a person under 18 years of age to play a game of skill
1446 machine and shall designate an employee to regularly monitor the designated area where game of
1447 skill machines are played to ensure that no person under 18 years of age is playing or attempting
1448 to play a game of skill machine;
1449 “(2) Verify that each person playing a game of skill machine is lawfully permitted
1450 to do so by checking the person’s government-issued identification document upon entry into
1451 either the licensed establishment or the designated area where the game of skill machines are
1452 located and where the person seeks to cash out his or her winnings, if any; except, that the failure
1453 of a licensee to verify a person’s identification shall not be a violation of this paragraph if the
1454 person whose identification was not checked is 18 years of age or older;
1455 “(3) Not allow or permit a person that appears intoxicated or under the influence
1456 of a narcotic or other substance to play a game of skill machine;
1457 “(4) Not share revenue from the licensee’s sale of alcohol with a manufacturer or
1458 distributor of a game of skill machine, unless approved by the Board as an owner of the license;
1459 “(5) Not allow or permit the placement of a game of skill machine on an outdoor
1460 public or private space that has not been approved by the Board;
1461 “(6) Not allow or permit the placement of a game of skill machine outside of the
1462 designated areas contained on the applicant’s diagram provided as part of the license application
1463 or outside the areas approved by the Board;
1464 “(7) Not have more than 5 game of skill machines on the licensed premises; and
65

1465 “(8) Install security cameras that are operational and record for 30 days, in the
1466 areas designated for game of skill machines, near the cash register or terminal where cash
1467 winnings of game of skill machines are processed, and where the licensee’s money is stored.
1468 “§ 25-789. Card gaming operating requirements.
1469 “A licensee with a card gaming endorsement shall:
1470 “(1) Not allow or permit a person under 18 years of age to participate in card
1471 gaming and shall designate an employee to regularly monitor the designated area where card
1472 gaming is located to ensure that no person under 18 years of age is participating or attempting to
1473 participate in card gaming;
1474 “(2) Verify that each person participating in card gaming is lawfully permitted to
1475 do so by checking the person’s government-issued identification document upon entry into either
1476 the licensed establishment or the designated area where card gaming is located and where the
1477 person seeks to cash out his or her winnings, if any; except, that the failure of a licensee to verify
1478 a person’s identification shall not be a violation of this paragraph if the person whose
1479 identification was not checked is 18 years of age or older;
1480 “(3) Not allow or permit a person that appears intoxicated or under the influence
1481 of a narcotic or other substance to participate in card gaming;
1482 “(4) Not share revenue from the licensee’s sale of alcohol with a card gaming
1483 operator, unless approved by the Board as an owner of the license;
1484 “(5) Not allow or permit card gaming outside of the areas approved by the Board;
1485 “(6) Install security cameras that are operational and record for 30 days, in the
1486 areas designated for card gaming, near the cash register or terminal where cash winnings of card
1487 gaming are processed, and where the licensee’s money is stored.
66

1508 follows:
1509 “(15A) “Commercial bingo” means a bingo game for which any type of
1510 consideration is paid or collected to play, but does not include a bingo game sponsored,
67

1511 conducted, or held by an entity in accordance with section 24(b), (c), or (d) of the Law to
1512 Legalize Lotteries, Daily Numbers Games, and Bingo and Raffles for Charitable Purposes in the
1513 District of Columbia, effective March 10, 1981 (D.C. Law 3-172; D.C. Official Code § 36-
1514 601.23(b), (c), or(d)).

1517 “(h) A licensee under an on-premises retailer’s license class C/R, D/R, C/T, D/T, C/H,
1518 D/H, C/X, D/X, C/RB, D/RB, C/N, or D/N, shall, in order to offer commercial bingo on the

1528 Sec. 2073. The Law to Legalize Lotteries, Daily Numbers Games, and Bingo and Raffles
1529 for Charitable Purposes in the District of Columbia, effective March 10, 1981 (D.C. Law 3-172;
1530 D.C. Official Code passim), is amended as follows:
1531 (a) Section 2 (D.C. Official Code § 36-601.01) is amended as follows:
1532 (1) Subsection (c) is amended as follows:
1533 (A) Paragraph (1) is redesignated as paragraph (1B).
68

1534 (B) New paragraphs (1) and (1A) are added to read as follows:
1535 “(1) “Bingo” means:
1536 “(A) A form of gambling in which the winning chances are determined by
1537 a random drawing of a subset of numbered objects among a total set of 75 objects, consecutively
1538 numbered from 1 to 75, and the bingo cards held by the players, which cards are sold, rented, or
1539 used only at the time of the gambling activity; or
1540 “(B) Electronic bingo.
1541 “(1A) “Bingo card” means a card, including paper formats, electronic
1542 representations, and image formats, that contains 5 rows of 5 spaces each, each space imprinted
1543 with a number between 1 and 75 inclusive, except the central space which is marked “FREE”.”.

1846 SUBTITLE P. ZONING DECISION APPEALS
1847 Sec. 2151. Short title.
1848 This subtitle may be cited as the “Zoning Decision Appeals Amendment Act of 2025”.
82

1849 Sec. 2152. Section 11 of the District of Columbia Administrative Procedure Act,
1850 approved October 21, 1968 (82 Stat. 1209; D.C. Official Code § 2-510), is amended by adding a
1851 new subsection (a-1) to read as follows:
1852 “(a-1)(1) Judicial review under this section of an order or decision of the Zoning
1853 Commission, the Board of Zoning Adjustment, or the Mayor’s Agent shall only be available to a
1854 person who:
1855 “(A)(i) Was granted party status by the Zoning Commission, Board of
1856 Zoning Adjustment, or Mayor’s Agent in the contested case for which the person seeks judicial
1857 review;
1858 “(ii) Owns or legally occupies a property within 200 feet of the
1859 property that is the subject of the contested case and filed a letter of support, opposition, or of no
1860 position in the contested case; or
1861 “(iii) For the purposes of judicial review of an order or decision of
1862 the Mayor’s Agent, is a historic preservation organization as defined in 10-C DCMR § 9901;
1863 “(B) Files a petition for judicial review within 30 days after the order or
1864 decision is mailed or emailed to the person by the Zoning Commission, the Board of Zoning
1865 Adjustment, or the Mayor’s Agent to the person, 30 days after the date the decision or order is
1866 published in the District of Columbia Register, or 30 days after the date the decision or order is
1867 published on a website of the District government, whichever comes first, unless a later date is
1868 consented to by all respondents listed in the petition for review; and
1869 “(C) Pleads, in its petition for judicial review, specific facts sufficient to
1870 support the existence of a particularized harm suffered by the person and that:
83

1871 “(i) Substantial evidence of the particularized harm was presented
1872 to the Zoning Commission, the Board of Zoning Adjustment, or the Mayor’s Agent during the
1873 contested case;
1874 “(ii) The person’s particularized harm relates to the zoning relief
1875 granted or denied;
1876 (iii) The person’s particularized harm is not shared by the general
1877 public; and
1878 “(iv) The particularized harm is capable of being redressed by a
1879 favorable decision by the Court.
1880 “(2) The Court shall not have jurisdiction under subsection (a) of this section of a
1881 petition for judicial review of an order or decision of the Zoning Commission, the Board of
1882 Zoning Adjustment, or the Mayor’s Agent that does not satisfy the requirements set forth in
1883 paragraph (1) of this subsection.
1884 “(3)(A) The Court may, upon the motion of a party or intervenor in the appeal
1885 who is the person in whose favor the order or decision in the contested case was issued (the
1886 “prevailing party in the zoning decision”), require a person who filed a petition for judicial
1887 review covered by this subsection (the “petitioner”) to file a bond of sufficient surety in an
1888 amount the Court considers proper, not to exceed $250,000, to indemnify the prevailing party in
1889 the zoning decision against damages which such party may sustain due to delays caused by the
1890 appeal; provided, that the likelihood and estimated amount of damages is substantiated in the
1891 motion. In deciding whether to require such a bond and determining the amount of the bond, if
1892 any, the Court shall consider the goal of discouraging frivolous and vexatious appeals, the goal
1893 of not discouraging meritorious appeals, the extent to which the delays caused by the appeal may
84

1894 harm the public interest, the ability of the petitioner to pay the bond and the financial burden of
1895 the payment relative to the petitioner’s means, and the apparent meritoriousness of the appeal.
1896 “(B) If the order or decision in the contested case is affirmed by the Court,
1897 the Court may, if a bond was required under subparagraph (A) of this paragraph and upon the
1898 motion of the prevailing party in the zoning decision, order the petitioner to pay to the prevailing
1899 party in the zoning decision an amount the Court considers proper to compensate the prevailing
1900 party in the zoning decision for the damages it sustained due to delays caused by the appears;
1901 provided, that the amount ordered to be paid shall not exceed $250,000. In determining whether
1902 to order such a payment, and the amount of such payment to award, if any, the Court shall
1903 consider the extent to which the prevailing party in the zoning decision has substantiated that it
1904 sustained damages due to delays caused by the appeal, whether the delays caused by the appeal
1905 harmed the public interest, the goal of discouraging frivolous and vexatious appeals, the goal of
1906 not discouraging meritorious appeals, the ability of the petitioner to make the payment and the
1907 financial burden of the payment relative to the petitioner’s means, and the meritoriousness of the
1908 appeal.
1909 “(4) If the order or decision is affirmed by the Court and the Court finds that the
1910 appeal was frivolous or filed for an improper purpose, such as to harass or to cause unnecessary
1911 delay, the Court may order the petitioner to reimburse to the prevailing party in the zoning
1912 decision reasonable attorney’s fees and other costs incurred by it in defending against the appeal
1913 in an amount not to exceed $50,000.
1914 “(4) For the purposes of this subsection, the term “Mayor’s Agent” means a
1915 person designated by the Mayor to issue orders or decisions in contested cases pursuant to the
1916 Historic Landmark and Historic District Protection Act of 1978, effective March 3, 1979 (D.C.
85

1917 Law 2-144; D.C. Official Code § 6-1101 et seq.), or the individual to whom such person has
1918 delegated the authority to issue orders or decisions in such contested cases.”.

2013 Sec. 2173. Findings.
2014 (a) The RFK Campus consists of approximately 180 acres of waterfront property located
2015 in the District within Reservation 343F, as shown on the transfer of jurisdiction plat recorded in
2016 the Surveyor’s Office on February 5, 2025, on page 13 of subdivision book 223. The District has
2017 been unable to redevelop the site over the last decade due to federal restrictions on development
2018 at the site, and the site has remained vacant, blighted, and fallow. Over the course of the last
2019 decade, the District has worked to gain broader control of the site and remove the federal
2020 development restrictions so that a new, multi-use future for the area could be realized.
2021 (b) With bipartisan support from Congress, the President signed Public Law 118-274, the
2022 D.C. Robert F. Kennedy Memorial Stadium Campus Revitalization Act, into law on January 6,
2023 2025. Pursuant to this law, the National Park Service transferred administrative jurisdiction over
2024 the RFK Campus to the District. The Council approved the transfer of jurisdiction pursuant to the
2025 Transfer of Jurisdiction Over the Robert F. Kennedy Memorial Stadium Campus Emergency
2026 Approval Resolution of 2025, effective February 4, 2025 (Res. 26-16; 72 DCR 1436).
2027 (c) The District now has a once-in-a-generation opportunity to continue to revitalize the
2028 Anacostia Waterfront, catalyze growth, and develop a vibrant, mixed-use development featuring
2029 community sports, professional sports, public recreation, public park space, and cultural
90

2030 amenities. The development will provide the District with significant economic, cultural, social,
2031 and financial benefits.
2032 (d) Since gaining administrative jurisdiction over the RFK Campus, the District
2033 government has undertaken a comprehensive public engagement process, considering the
2034 specific interests of communities near the RFK Campus; economic development opportunities;
2035 the capacity of the campus to generate jobs for District residents and opportunities for District
2036 businesses; park, open space, and recreational options; river access options; potential community
2037 amenities; opportunities to create new housing units; and environmental and historical factors,
2038 among other considerations, to determine the best uses for the site.
2039 (e) Considering the public input received, the existing infrastructure of the campus, and
2040 the possibility of a catalytic investment in the District, it was determined that the construction
2041 and operation of a new first-class, state-of-the-art, sports stadium with supporting facilities,
2042 including parking, and infrastructure, for use by the professional football franchise owned by
2043 Pro-Football LLC, and an adjacent Sportsplex would be of considerable public benefit to the
2044 District as the first stage of the redevelopment and revitalization of the entire campus.
2045 (f) To ensure delivery of the Stadium, supporting facilities, and Sportsplex by 2030, a
2046 limited zoning exemption is necessary for the RFK Campus.
2047 (g) Planning for other residential and commercial development at the RFK Campus, in
2048 addition to other uses permitted by the transfer of jurisdiction and the Declaration of Covenants,
2049 will continue as the Stadium and Sportsplex projects move forward, and will inform the
2050 Comprehensive Plan rewrite (DC 2050).
2051 (h) The District intends for the comprehensive redevelopment of the RFK Campus to
2052 create a vibrant, multi-use community and destination that will create new jobs, business
91

2053 opportunities, housing, community amenities, and neighborhood-serving retail and achieve the 5
2054 Anacostia Waterfront Framework Plan themes: (1) a clean and active river, (2) gaining access to,
2055 along, and across the river, (3) a great riverfront park system, (4) a riverfront of distinct places
2056 and cultural destinations, and (5) building and sustaining strong waterfront neighborhoods.
2057 (i) The District and Pro-Football LLC have entered into a term sheet for the development
2058 of the Stadium and supporting facilities and the redevelopment of a portion of the RFK Campus
2059 that sets forth the terms and conditions upon which the parties are willing to undertake the
2060 projects.
2061 (j) The construction, development, and revitalization of the RFK Campus and the public
2062 ownership of the Stadium, for use for athletic and entertainment events, is a municipal use that is
2063 in the interest of, and for the benefit of, District residents because such a publicly-owned
2064 Stadium will contribute to the social and economic well-being of District residents and
2065 significantly enhance economic development and employment opportunities in the District.
2066 (k) To further that interest, it is appropriate for the District to take certain actions with
2067 respect to the redevelopment of the RFK Campus, as further set forth in this act.
2068 Sec. 2174. Development and Financing Agreement.
2069 Neither the Procurement Practices Reform Act of 2010, effective April 8, 2011 (D.C.
2070 Law 18-371; D.C. Official Code § 2-351.01 et seq.), the Public-Private Partnership Act of 2014,
2071 effective March 11, 2015 (D.C. Law 20-228; D.C. Official Code § 2-271.01 et seq.), nor any
2072 other District law shall apply to the Development and Financing Agreement or any other
2073 agreement the Mayor may from time to time enter into, as the Mayor may determine to be
2074 necessary or appropriate, in furtherance of the purposes of the Development and Financing
2075 Agreement; except that, notwithstanding the dollar value of government assistance to be received
92

2076 pursuant to the Development and Financing Agreement, the following statutory provisions shall
2077 apply to the construction obligations of the Developer under the Development and Financing
2078 Agreement:
2079 (a) The First Source Employment Agreement Act of 1984 (“First Source Act”), effective
2080 June 29, 1984 (D.C. Law 5-93; D.C. Official Code §§ 2-219.01 et seq.), with a preference for at
2081 least 20% of the new jobs created in connection with the Stadium Project designated for
2082 residents in Wards 7 or 8;
2083 (b) Section 5 of the Amendments to An Act To Provide for Voluntary Apprenticeship in
2084 the District of Columbia Act of 1978, effective March 6, 1979 (D.C. Law 2-156; D.C. Official
2085 Code § 32-1431); and
2086 (c) The Small, Local, and Disadvantaged Business Enterprise Development and
2087 Assistance Act of 2005, effective October 20, 2005 (D.C. Law 16-33; D.C. Official Code § 2-
2088 218.01 et seq.), with a preference for at least 10% of the certified business enterprises located in
2089 Wards 7 or 8.
2090 Sec. 2175. Lease of the Development Site; easements over the RFK Campus; sale of
2091 Stadium Seat Rights.
2092 (a) Notwithstanding An Act Authorizing the sale of certain real estate in the District of
2093 Columbia no longer required for public purposes, approved August 5, 1939 (53 Stat. 1211; D.C.
2094 Official Code § 10-801 et seq.), the Mayor may:
2095 (1) Dispose of the Development Site by lease pursuant to the terms of the Term
2096 Sheet;
2097 (2) Sell Stadium Seat Rights to the Developer pursuant to the terms of the Term
2098 Sheet; and
93

2099 (3) Grant easements over the RFK Campus to such persons as the Mayor
2100 determines appropriate in furtherance of the redevelopment of the RFK Campus.
2101 (b) Any revenue received by the District from the sale of the Stadium Seat Rights,
2102 including revenue received by an instrumentality or authority of the District pursuant to an
2103 assignment or transfer of the authority to sell Stadium Seat Rights pursuant to section 2166, shall
2104 be dedicated to and expended only for the purposes for which such revenue may be expended
2105 under the Term Sheet.

2107 Rights.
